∼(sbid ∈dom(res) ∧segment ∈res(sbid)) ∧
(sbid ∈dom(sboxes) ∨sbid ∈rng(sboxes)) ∧
segment ∈segments_of_route(route),
−−Restricted version of reservation guard for trains . The
−−switchbox must be the next switchbox and the segment to be

(sbid = nextsb ∨
(nextsb ∈dom(sboxes) ∧sbid = sboxes(nextsb))) ∧
seg(pos) ∈dom(route) ∧segment = route(seg(pos)),
−−Checks whether it is possible for a train to reserve a given

res(seg) = t_none,
−−Checks whether a train is allowed to lock a point at a
−−switchbox with the given ID. The train cannot have already
−−locked the point. The point can be locked if the switchbox is
−−one of the switchboxes along the train’s route (except for
−−the last switchbox, which should never be locked, since the
−−train will never pass that switchbox). The train can only
−−lock a switchbox to some (key,value)−pair in the train’s
−−route, so the requested connection should match a
−−(key,value)−pair from the route. The train must have
−−reservations for both the segments of the connection at the

−−switchbox.

c = conn(seg,route(seg)) ∧sbid ∈dom(res) ∧
route(seg) ∈res(sbid) ∧

−−Checks whether a train is allowed to switch a point at a

route(seg) ∈res(sbid) ∧
seg ∈res(sbid )),
−−Restricted and merged version of switch and lock guard for
−−trains. The switch and lock can only be made at the next

−−Checks whether a switchbox can lock a point for a given train

sb_can_lock : Connection × Connection × TrainID →Bool

−−Checks whether a switchbox can switch a point. This is the

/∗SAFETY ∗/
−−Checks that two trains do not collide by checking if the sets
−−of segments of their positions intersect .
no_collide : TrainID × TrainID × TPosState →Bool
no_collide(tid1,tid2,tPosState) ≡
tid1 ∈dom(tPosState) ∧tid2 ∈dom(tPosState) ∧
tid1 ̸= tid2 ∧
segments_of_pos(tPosState(tid1)) ∩
segments_of_pos(tPosState(tid2)) = {},
−−Checks that a train is not derailed . Derailment happens if a
−−train is in a critical
section (i .e. double position) and the
−−two segments are not connected by any switchbox.

∼is_single_pos(pos) ∧
are_conn_by_sb(seg1(pos),seg2(pos),sbconns),

−−Move from a single position to a double position. Only the
−−position and sensor are updated.
([=] tid : TrainID •
[move_single]
is_single_pos(tPos(tid)) ∧
t_can_move(seg(tPos(tid)),tRoute(tid),tLocks(tid),tNextsb(tid),
tRes(tid),tSboxes(tid)) =⇒
tPos′(tid) = t_move_pos_single(tPos(tid),tRoute(tid)),
sbSensor′(tNextsb(tid)) = active)
[=]
−−Move from a double position to a single position. The segment
−−which the train is leaving is removed from the route, the switchbox
−−which has just been passed is removed from the switchboxes, the
−−next switchboxis updated accordingly, and the reservations and
−−the locks from the switchbox which is passed are removed.
([=] tid : TrainID •

[move_double]
∼is_single_pos(tPos(tid)) =⇒

tSboxes′(tid) = t_move_sboxes(tNextsb(tid),tSboxes(tid)),
tNextsb′(tid) = t_move_nextsb(tNextsb(tid),tSboxes(tid)),

[=]
−−Update the train position to the same as it was when the train
−−has reached the end of its route. Just prevents deadlocks when

([=] tid : TrainID •
[move_end]
tRoute(tid) = [] =⇒
tPos′(tid) = tPos(tid))
[=]
−−Reserve a segment at a switchbox where the train already has a
−−reservation. The reservations of the train and the switchboxes
−−are updated.
([=] sbid : SwitchboxID, tid : TrainID, seg : Segment •
[res_sbin]

t_can_reserve(tSboxes(tid),sbid,seg,tRoute(tid),tRes(tid)) ∧

[=]
−−Reserve a segment at a switchbox where the train does not
−−already have a reservation. The reservations of the train and
−−the switchboxes are updated.
([=] sbid : SwitchboxID, tid : TrainID, seg : Segment •
[res_sbnotin]
sbid /∈dom(tRes(tid)) ∧
t_can_reserve(tSboxes(tid),sbid,seg,tRoute(tid),tRes(tid)) ∧
sb_can_reserve(sbRes(sbid),seg) =⇒
tRes′(tid) = t_res_sb_notin(tRes(tid),sbid,seg),
sbRes′(sbid) = sb_res(sbRes(sbid),tid,seg))
[=]
−−Switch a point to suit the connection desired by the train . The
==PAGE:182==

A Generic Specifications
−−connection of the switchbox is updated.

tLocks(tid)) ∧

switchboxes) =⇒
sbConn′(sbid) = c)

Model V2
Base
scheme V2 = extend Base with
class
transition_system
[TS]
local
tRoute : TRouteState,
tPos : TPosState,
tNextsb : TNextsbState,
tSboxes : TSboxesState,
tRes : TResState,
tLocks : TLocksState,
sbConn : SbConnState,
sbLock : SbLockState,
sbSensor : SbSensorState,
sbRes : SbResState,
resAction : Bool := false,
==PAGE:184==
168
A Generic Specifications
switchAction : Bool := false,
lockAction : Bool := false,
tmpSeg : Segment,
tmpConn : Connection,
req : TrainID →
m SwitchboxID := [],
ack : SwitchboxID →
m TrainID := [],
nack : SwitchboxID →
m TrainID := []
in
−−Move from a single position to a double position. Only the
−−position and sensor are updated.
([=] tid : TrainID •
[move_single]
∼resAction ∧∼lockAction ∧∼switchAction ∧
is_single_pos(tPos(tid)) ∧
t_can_move(seg(tPos(tid)),tRoute(tid),tLocks(tid),tNextsb(tid),
tRes(tid),tSboxes(tid)) =⇒
tPos′(tid) = t_move_pos_single(tPos(tid),tRoute(tid)),
sbSensor′(tNextsb(tid)) = active)
[=]
−−Move from a double position to a single position. The segment
−−which the train is leaving is removed from the route, the switchbox
−−which has just been passed is removed from the switchboxes, the
−−next switchboxis updated accordingly, and the reservations and
−−the locks from the switchbox which is passed are removed.
([=] tid : TrainID •
[move_double]
∼resAction ∧∼lockAction ∧∼switchAction ∧
∼is_single_pos(tPos(tid)) =⇒
tRoute′(tid) = t_move_route(seg1(tPos(tid)),tRoute(tid)),
tPos′(tid) = t_move_pos_double(tPos(tid),tRoute(tid)),
tSboxes′(tid) = t_move_sboxes(tNextsb(tid),tSboxes(tid)),
tNextsb′(tid) = t_move_nextsb(tNextsb(tid),tSboxes(tid)),
tRes′(tid) = t_move_res(tNextsb(tid),tRes(tid)),
tLocks′(tid) = t_move_locks(tNextsb(tid),tLocks(tid)),
sbSensor′(tNextsb(tid)) = passive,
sbRes′(tNextsb(tid)) = sb_move_reservations(tPos(tid),
sbRes(tNextsb(tid))),
sbLock′(tNextsb(tid)) = t_none)
[=]
−−Update the train position to the same as it was when the train
−−has reached the end of its route. Just prevents deadlocks when
==PAGE:185==
A.3 Model V2
169
−−there is nothing more to do.
([=] tid : TrainID •
[move_end]
∼resAction ∧∼lockAction ∧∼switchAction ∧
tRoute(tid) = [] ∧tid ̸= t_none =⇒
tPos′(tid) = tPos(tid))
[=]
−−Train requests a reservation for a specific segment (tmpSeg) by
−−setting a request variable .
([=] sbid : SwitchboxID, tid : TrainID, seg : Segment •
[req_res]
∼resAction ∧∼lockAction ∧∼switchAction ∧
t_can_reserve(tSboxes(tid),sbid,seg,tRoute(tid),tRes(tid)) ∧
tid /∈dom(req) =⇒
req′ = req † [ tid 7→sbid],
resAction′ = true,
tmpSeg′ = seg)
[=]
−−Switchbox can acknowledge reservation if allowed and updates
−−its state space with the reservation .
([=] sbid : SwitchboxID, tid : TrainID •
[ack_res]
tid ∈dom(req) ∧req(tid) = sbid ∧resAction ∧
sb_can_reserve(sbRes(sbid),tmpSeg) =⇒
req′ = req \ {tid},
ack′ = ack † [sbid 7→tid],
sbRes′(sbid) = sb_res(sbRes(sbid),tid,tmpSeg))
[=]
−−Switchbox can send negative acknowledgement if not allowed to
−−make the reservation.
([=] sbid : SwitchboxID, tid : TrainID •
[nack_res]
tid ∈dom(req) ∧req(tid) = sbid ∧resAction ∧
∼sb_can_reserve(sbRes(sbid),tmpSeg) =⇒
req′ = req \ {tid},
nack′ = nack † [sbid 7→tid])
[=]
−−The negative acknowledgement is ”consumed” and the failed
−−reservation action is ended.
([=] sbid : SwitchboxID, tid : TrainID •
[end_res]
sbid ∈dom(nack) ∧nack(sbid) = tid ∧resAction =⇒
nack′ = nack \ {sbid},
resAction′ = false)

TS ⊢(∀tid : TrainID •
G (tid ̸= t_none ⇒route_wf(tRoute(tid),network))),
[wf_pos]
TS ⊢(∀tid : TrainID •
G (pos_wf(tPos(tid),network))),
[wf_train_sbs]
TS ⊢(∀tid : TrainID •
G (train_sbs_wf(tSboxes(tid),switchboxes))),
[wf_sb_connection] TS ⊢(∀sbid : SwitchboxID •
G(sb_connection_wf(sbid,sbConn(sbid),
switchboxes))),
−−CONSISTENT
[c_sbs_route]
TS ⊢(∀tid : TrainID •
G(train_sbs_route_consistent(tSboxes(tid),
tRoute(tid),switchboxes))),
[c_pos_route]
TS ⊢(∀tid : TrainID •
G(consistent_pos(tPos(tid),tRoute(tid)))),
[c_nextsb_pos]
TS ⊢(∀tid : TrainID •
G(consistent_next_sb(tNextsb(tid),tPos(tid),
tSboxes(tid),switchboxes))),
[c_res_route]
TS ⊢(∀tid : TrainID •
G(tid ̸= t_none ⇒
consistent_t_reservations(tRes(tid),tRoute(tid)))),
[c_locks_sbs]
TS ⊢(∀tid : TrainID •
G(consistent_t_locks(tLocks(tid),tSboxes(tid)))),
[c_res]
TS ⊢(∀sbid : SwitchboxID, tid : TrainID •
G(∼resAction ∧∼switchLockAction
⇒(cons_sb_t_res(tid,sbid,tRes,sbRes) ∧
cons_t_sb_res(tid,sbid,tRes,sbRes)))),
==PAGE:195==
A.4 Model V3
179
[c_locks]
TS ⊢G(∼resAction ∧∼switchLockAction
⇒cons_locks(tLocks,sbLock)),
[c_sensor_pos]
TS ⊢G(cons_sensor(tPos,tNextsb,sbSensor,
switchboxes)),
−−ACTIONS EVENTUALLY END
[ finish_res ]
TS ⊢G(resAction ⇒F(∼resAction)),
[finish_switchlock]
TS ⊢G(switchLockAction ⇒
F(∼switchLockAction))
end

only be the configuration data, i.e. only the few lines which should be changed

dummy data for tmpSeg and tmpConn.
tmpSeg : Segment := s1,

APPENDIX C
SML Tests
This appendix contains the file with configurations and test cases which was
translated to SML in order to run the test cases. The test results are also shown.
C.1
Test Cases and Scenario
Base
scheme Test = extend Base with
class
value
−−Checks whether all consistency functions hold.
consistent : TPosState × TRouteState × TNextsbState ×
TSboxesState × TResState × TLocksState ×
SbConnState × SbLockState × SbSensorState ×
SbResState × SwitchboxDesc →Bool
consistent(pos,route,nextsb,sboxes,tres , tlocks ,conn,sblock,sensor,sbres,
sbdesc) ≡
(∀tid : TrainID • tid ∈dom(pos) ⇒
train_sbs_route_consistent(sboxes(tid),route(tid),sbdesc) ∧
consistent_pos(pos(tid),route(tid)) ∧
consistent_next_sb(nextsb(tid),pos(tid),sboxes(tid ),sbdesc) ∧
consistent_t_reservations(tres(tid ),route(tid)) ∧
consistent_t_locks(tlocks(tid ),sboxes(tid))) ∧
cons_res(tres,sbres) ∧
cons_locks(tlocks,sblock) ∧
cons_sensor(pos,nextsb,sensor,sbdesc),

APPENDIX G
The Simplest System
Model
This appendix contains the simplest system model which was used as a starting
point for the modelling process.
scheme First =
class
type
Segment == s1 | s2 | s3 | s4,
Connection ::
seg1 : Segment
seg2 : Segment,
Route = Segment →
m Segment,
Network = Connection-set,
Train ::
pos : Segment
route :
Route
value
empty : Route = [],
network : Network = {mk_Connection(s1,s2),mk_Connection(s1,s3),
mk_Connection(s2,s4),mk_Connection(s3,s4)},
−−Trains can move if their route is in accordance with the network,
−−i.e. if the next step in the route is contained in the network as a
−−connection.
can_move : Train × Network →Bool
can_move(t,net) ≡pos(t) ∈dom(route(t)) ∧
mk_Connection(pos(t),route(t)(pos(t))) ∈net
transition_system
[TS]
local
train_pos : Segment := s1,
==PAGE:322==
306
G The Simplest System Model
train_route : Route := [s1 7→s2, s2 7→s4]
in
−−Update the train position and route when the train moves.
[move]
can_move(mk_Train(train_pos,train_route),network) =⇒
train_pos′ = train_route(train_pos),
train_route′ = train_route \ {train_pos}
[=]
−−Prevent deadlock when the train reaches its destination.
[end_update]
train_route = empty =⇒
train_pos′ = s4
end
ltl_assertion
−−Never go to s3 (which is not in the route).
[never_s3] TS ⊢G(train_pos ̸= s3),
−−Never reach s4 (final segment in route). Should produce a counter
−−example showing that the train can eventually reach s4.
[destination] TS ⊢G(train_pos ̸= s4),
−−When reaching s4 the route should be empty, i.e. there should be
−−no more moves to take.
[empty_route] TS ⊢train_pos = s4 ⇒train_route = empty
end
==PAGE:323==
APPENDIX H
E-mail from Chris
George
> Sorry, but I really don't have any quantitative feel for this.
All I
> can offer are some guidelines I learned from Mondex about making it
> more checkable:
>
> - If your state contains some records then split into separate state
> components, so you have more variables in the transition system
>
> - Split the transition system when you can by effectively unfolding
> the top level functions, when the splits will affect fewer state
> variables
>
> eg if you have a top level function f of the form
>
> f(...) is if c then a else b end
> pre p
>
> then instead of one transition
>
> p ==> s' = f(s)
>
> have two
>
> p /\ c ==> s' = a(s)
> [=]
> p /\ ~c ==> s' = b(s)
>
> where of course s' = ... each time is really a collection of state
> updates, and the split ones are smaller collections than the original
> ones (because you don't include the updates that leave the variable
> unchanged).
>
> - Another technique I used for Mondex was to encode the PayDetails
> type into an integer in the range 0..31 (PayDetailsIndex).
In the
==PAGE:324==
308
H E-mail from Chris George
> version checking invariants I had some assertions that involved
> quantifiers over this type:
>
> G(all i : PayDetailsIndex :- ...)
>
> I split the type PayDetailsIndex into 4 quarters, 0..7, 8 .. 15 etc,
> and split some assertions into 4 assertions, one for each quarter.
>
> - You can sometimes run SAL on just one assertion at a time when
> taking all of them gets too big.
So for the invariant checks I split
> the conjuncts in the invariants into separate assertions and then run
> SAL by a script that checks each assertion in turn: see the attached
> script.
>
> - I added some extra variables where this simplified the calculations.
> Eg to check that the money circulating did not increase I added
> totalCirculating and previousTotalCirculating and explicitly updated
> them in each transition:
>
> previousTotalCirculating' = totalCirculating,
> totalCirculating'
>
=
>
inPurses(purse1', purse2') +
>
inTransit(purse1', purse2', log1', log2'))
>
> I could if necessary have added two more variables, to memoise
> inPurses and inTransit, and then perhaps split the records for each
> purse: balance1, etc.
>
> Using purse1 and purse2, and logs separate from the purses. instead of
> a map PurseNo -m-> Purse is an example of the first step, and then
> also splitting the transitions so that I removed a choice over two
> purses by having two transitions, one for purse1 and one for purse2.
> The first only changes purse1 and log1, the other only changes purse2
> and log2.
I also further split some transitions into those that
> changed the logs and those that didn't.
>
> Similarly the ether was split into 3 sets, one for each kind of
> message, since transitions only affected at most one of these sets.
>
> - I had a separate top level specification for checking invariants
> because the latter did not need some variables (lost,
> totalCirculating, previousTotalCirculating) that the safety conditions
> needed.
(I should have tried having two transition systems in one
> specification.)
>
> The problem is that all these manipulations need to be justified,
==PAGE:325==
H E-mail from Chris George
309
> which either means proof or very careful checking!
So you try running
> SAL on the original specification, and then if it can't manage (it
> runs out of memory) you keep trying them until it succeeds.
That way
> you at least minimise the changes.
>
> Overall, the lesson seems to be that it is not just the raw size of
> the state space in terms of number of variables that is important.
> Having more variables, and splitting transitions so that each only
> affects a few of them, is the way to go.
>
> Incidentally, remember to change the numbers in SAL_GLOBAL.sal to the
> bounds you need for the specification.
Otherwise you may get spurious
> cc violations when an Int or Nat is out of bounds.
Unfortunately you
> need to redo this each time you recompile.
I haven't thought of a
> good way to do this automatically.
